        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354498003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1097475809127870751">3.75 stars<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm scared," I tell him, "of what I feel when I'm around you. I'm scared of what I want from you, and I don't know how to ask for it."</i>
    <b></b>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This book is so fluffy and at the same time, confusing for me. I liked it because it just has the right amount of cheesiness that I love, and Porter—oh my gosh—that boy was just what my heart needs. I think people who will get to reading this will absolutely know from the start what is going to happen in this book and while that has som</span>
  <span id="freeText1097475809127870751" style="display:none">3.75 stars<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm scared," I tell him, "of what I feel when I'm around you. I'm scared of what I want from you, and I don't know how to ask for it."</i>
    <b></b>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This book is so fluffy and at the same time, confusing for me. I liked it because it just has the right amount of cheesiness that I love, and Porter—oh my gosh—that boy was just what my heart needs. I think people who will get to reading this will absolutely know from the start what is going to happen in this book and while that has some pros and cons, I think the pros won me over. I just wish the thinly veiled plot twist had steered on a higher note, not to the exit with the flashing red signs that obviously says, EXIT. The predictability is one of the things I absolutely didn't like in this book.<br /><br />Although I like that this book tried to explore PTSD in a more approachable way, I just find it a bit disappointing that the story didn't delve into that matter deeper, in a way that they could have asked for some help and talk to other people about it. Love won't make mental illness go away and that's an aspect of this book that I found lacking and dismaying.<br /><br />And even if I really enjoyed this book, it's confusing that it took me more than two weeks to finish it and that I had a mini-slump specific to this book. I guess there were just some plodding moments that could have honestly go away and would make the book instantly better. Or maybe that's just me.</span>

<div id="review_1802662888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802662888" />
    <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books"><img alt="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527965221p2/19967008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802662888?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books">Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481478793" href="/book/show/30313265-alex-approximately">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-publisher">netgalley-edelweiss-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802662888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12604869021864454141">Alex, Approximately is a modern re-telling of You’ve Got Mail. I love that movie, so I knew I needed to read this book! Seventeen year old Bailey regularly chats on an online movie discussion group using the screen name Mink. She often chats with a boy who goes by the name Alex. Alex and Bailey’s dad live in the same city, but when Bailey makes the choice to move across the country to live with her father, she doesn’t tell Alex because she’s worried they won’t connect in real life. She decides s</span>
  <span id="freeText12604869021864454141" style="display:none">Alex, Approximately is a modern re-telling of You’ve Got Mail. I love that movie, so I knew I needed to read this book! Seventeen year old Bailey regularly chats on an online movie discussion group using the screen name Mink. She often chats with a boy who goes by the name Alex. Alex and Bailey’s dad live in the same city, but when Bailey makes the choice to move across the country to live with her father, she doesn’t tell Alex because she’s worried they won’t connect in real life. She decides she’ll find him first and then tell him.<br /><br />In the midst of that, she gets a summer job working at a museum with her extremely good looking yet extremely infuriating coworker, Porter. As she and Porter get to know each other, feelings start to develop. Little does she know that Porter is actually Alex, just as he has no idea that Bailey is actually Mink.<br /><br />I really loved this book – so much so that I actually read it in one sitting! It was just so cute! Obviously you know the basic plot if you’ve ever seen the movie, just replace the love of books shared in the movie to a love of classic film shared in the books.<br /><br />I adored the characters. There were definitely times I was like “COME ON! How can you not tell that it’s him?!” but I suppose the book would be very short and boring if she figured it out right away! Porter was probably my favorite character. I loved him so much! He was the right amount of sweet, sarcastic, and vulnerable that made me swoon! I loved that he and Bailey were both able to overcome the traumas that had happened to them in the past and gradually open up to each other.<br /><br />I also fell in love with the supporting characters. Bailey’s dad was the cutest, and I loved their relationship. He’s the type of dad every girl wants to have, and I love how close he and Bailey were. I also really liked Bailey’s friend Grace. She was sweet, and was really a good friend to Bailey.<br /><br />I definitely recommend Alex, Approximately for all fans of the YA genre! The one note I do want to make is that there are themes in the book that include masturbation, sex, drugs, and violence, so keep those in mind if you’re looking for a book that’s good for a younger teen.<br /><br />A huge thank you to Netgalley, Jenn Bennett, and the publisher Simon Pulse for the opportunity to read an advanced copy of the book in exchange for an honest review. Alex, Approximately has an expected publication date of April 4, 2017, so be sure to mark your calendars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12604869021864454141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1995181475" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995181475" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1995181475?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781534404946" href="/book/show/34927042-alex-approximately">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasmine by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/46487550-karen">Karen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=will-reread">will-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=happy-ending">happy-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=read-without-synopsis">read-without-synopsis</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1995181475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16777401795097320584"><b>
  <u><i>Alex, Approximately</i> is a book about two people who were meant to be together got lost and found, and lost and then found again.</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>Bailey “Mink” Rydell</b> was a seventeen-year-old “Artful Dodger,” who excelled in avoiding awkward moments or embarrassing conversations. In fact, she was a professional evader when it comes to reality and actual interaction with people. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That’s the thing about being an evader. You have to be flexible and know when to bail before it all gets weird. Better for eve</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16777401795097320584" style="display:none"><b>
  <u><i>Alex, Approximately</i> is a book about two people who were meant to be together got lost and found, and lost and then found again.</u>
</b><br><br><b>Bailey “Mink” Rydell</b> was a seventeen-year-old “Artful Dodger,” who excelled in avoiding awkward moments or embarrassing conversations. In fact, she was a professional evader when it comes to reality and actual interaction with people. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>That’s the thing about being an evader. You have to be flexible and know when to bail before it all gets weird. Better for everyone, really. I’m a giver.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Therefore, in order to express her inner feelings about life and stuff, she turned to a person named “Alex” from an online film fanatics community, whom she wasn’t even sure truly existed in the real world. At first, Alex invited her to the summer film festival on a California beach and asked her to fly there. Interestingly, Mink was about to move from Washington D.C. all the way to California so she planned to <s>stalk</s> “scope” on him before informing him of her visit. <br><br>After moving to California, Bailey/Mink started her summer job in a local museum and she met an adorable British girl, <b>Grace</b>, along with a cocky guy named <b>Porter Roth</b>, whose grandfather was a popular surfer. Needless to say, the more time Porter and Bailey spent with each other, the closer they got. However, during the times when Porter pissed Bailey off by embarrassing her in public (yeah, I’m talking about the speaker announcement *wink*) or making not-so-funny comments about her fashion style, she would distract herself by chatting with Alex online or putting more efforts into finding him in town. <br><br>Well, <b>never did she expect that Porter might <i>approximately</i> be Alex all this time.</b> How would they react to the truth? Would they still be able to get along? Or was that even true?<br><br>-----------------------------------<br>The first thing that captured my attention when opening this book is <b>the movie quotes for every single chapter</b>. The author was such a genius for picking out the best, if not the MOST EPIC, quotes from all the phenomenal movies in the history. You could find the most iconic films in different periods of time from the classics such as <i>Roman Holiday</i> to the modern musical comedy, <i>Pitch Perfect</i>. Such a wide variety of film choices fascinated me a lot and those quotes undoubtedly brought back some of the loveliest memories from my childhood (not that I’ve lived that long…you get what I mean!). <br><br><b>The most entertaining part in the story is definitely Porter and Bailey's encountering.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Or should I say, reunion? Since they’d been talking about movies and life and past relationships online for months, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I felt like the moment Porter showed up in Bailey’s life—despite the fact he actually irritated her in her first day of summer job—I knew he was so much more than just the plain, happy-go-lucky Porter. He was that Prince Charming in disguise with an outgoing personality on the outside but a darker, almost opposite version of him inside. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Maybe Walt Whitman was right. We all really do contradict ourselves and contain multitudes. How do we even figure out who we really are?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I really enjoyed reading this book because I was so eager to see Porter and Bailey’s development as friends and lovers. The author made this couple sound so adorable and I’ll tell you why. The following are my top three favorite scenes in this book:<br><br><b>
  <u>#3: <i>”Hello, Mink.”</i></u>
</b><br><p>At the end of the story, it was finally time to reveal these two online-lovers on a romantic, ten-thousand-times-better-than-the-East-Coast beach, so color my shock when Mink eventually found out who Alex, the one whom she trusted whole-heartedly this entire time, even when she complained about how terrible Porter was, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[was exactly, non-mistakenly, Porter “Alexander” Roth himself. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495549919ra/22829496.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No wonder Porter reacted like that when he accidentally heard Bailey’s nickname at game night and refused to talk to her for days because wow, I guess that’s what I’d feel if I were him.<b><i>”We’re basically cheating on each other with each other.”</i></b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><u>#2: <i>The Philadelphia Story</i></u></b><br></p><p>After Porter discovered the truth, he obviously overreacted and ignored her on purpose for awhile, but when she caught the “lurgy,” he turned out to be that knight in shining armor all of a sudden. *giggling* Porter was so cute when he insisted on staying with her in bed despite the germs and watched <s>Mink’s favorite movie</s>, <i>The Philadelphia Story</i>, starring Katharine Hepburn and Cary Grant. How lovely is that!</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495549919ra/22829498.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>#1: *drum rolls* <i>Bumblebee’s Lift &amp; moon muffins!</i></u>
</b><br><p>Nothing could beat this special <s>first date</s> moment of Porter and Bailey’s first hanging out when it comes to my favorite part of the story! Honestly, it’s probably one of the sweetest scenes I’ve ever read in YA contemporary novels. I was swooning over them so much that I can’t help but ship them all over again when I’m writing this review. </p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Delicately, I dip my hand into Porter’s gaping jacket until my fingertips hit the waxed-paper bag and find another muffin. It isn’t until I’m pulling it out that I look at Porter’s face and hesitate.<br>“No, please, go on,” he says. “Do help yourself.”<br>I give him a self-conscious grin.<br>“Oops.”<br>“You always go around sticking your hands down boys’ clothes?” he asks.<br>“When they’re full of baked goods.”<br>“Tomorrow I’m coming to work with ten pounds of pastries in my pants,” he mumbles to himself, making an ooaff! noise when I punch him lightly in the arm.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Do I need to say more!? This scene is literally the ultimate cuteness-overload. If you haven’t met Porter and Bailey yet, what are you waiting for???<br><br>Now that I’ve covered my favorite parts of the book, please allow me to point out something that’d been slightly bothering me while reading it. Frankly, I adored Porter and Bailey’s friendship-turned-relationship. They flirted a bit, chatted a lot and later realized that they had quite similar tastes in movies. <b>So apparently, the chemistry would work out naturally, right?<br><br>NOPE. TOTALLY NOT AS NATURALLY AS I PREFER.</b><br><br>If I remember correctly, they kissed fervently for the first time a few days after the Bumblebee’s Lift and honestly, Porter wasn’t so sure about what it was between them so he remained hot and cold. Later, they started to <s>do all the incredible things involving hands and fingers</s> touch each other at midnight in the museum (let me clarify, staying in the museum was an accident whereas <i>the other</i> part wasn’t). Well, their romance bloomed overnight and I personally thought spending a night in a closed museum was creepy enough, let alone getting intimate. Not long afterwards, they hit the homerun.<br><br>Well, I did not see that coming at all. So I was like…<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495549919ra/22829497.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No offense, I just didn’t like the speedy acceleration in their relationship. <b>Whatever they had before getting serious in the romance was oh so lovely; therefore, I personally thought the development after that kind of prelude to their romance was rushed and unnecessary. I’d appreciate more if the author could leave something to our imagination.</b> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Am I more afraid of Porter…or the person he’s unleashing inside me?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>All in all, <i>Alex, Approximately</i> is a book I <b>HIGHLY RECOMMEND</b> to everyone. It’s such a cute, light-hearted, swoon-worthy read and I finished the book with delight because of <i>that</i> ending. <b>If you’re still hesitant about picking this up, I promise you won’t be disappointed if you like YA Contemporary.</b> In fact, I’m positive that you’ll enjoy it as much as, if not more than, I did. Enough said, go read it, peeps! Immerse yourself in this wonderfully written story with Porter, Bailey/Mink, Alex, Grace and so many more lovable characters!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Two people who lived in two different places and found each other, not once but twice? You could stick one of us in Haiti and the other in a rocket headed to the moon and we’d still eventually be doing this right now.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>(P.S. Thank you to my dearest friend, Karen, for recommending this book to me. K, YOU’RE TRULY AMAZING!!!)</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16777401795097320584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading"><img alt="Kate (GirlReading)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504444998p2/29599654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268592023?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate (GirlReading)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate (GirlReading)" href="/user/show/29599654-kate-girlreading">Kate (GirlReading)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471161537" href="/book/show/31331865-alex-approximately">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=2018-favourites">2018-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268592023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer118065044184631985">4.5* With an adorable romance, film references, wonderful characters and the Californian sun, Jenn Bennett has once again written a winning contemporary with Alex, Approximately.<br/><br/>This was such an enjoyable read. The characters were witty and complex, with flaws and genuine personality. The multiple relationship dynamics were fantastic, from friendship to family to romance. Having visited a few of the locations in this book, my heart had a very happy surprise bringing me back to some wonderful hol</span>
  <span id="freeText118065044184631985" style="display:none">4.5* With an adorable romance, film references, wonderful characters and the Californian sun, Jenn Bennett has once again written a winning contemporary with Alex, Approximately.<br /><br />This was such an enjoyable read. The characters were witty and complex, with flaws and genuine personality. The multiple relationship dynamics were fantastic, from friendship to family to romance. Having visited a few of the locations in this book, my heart had a very happy surprise bringing me back to some wonderful holiday memories (although they'd admittedly be 10x better if I'd had a Porter...) One aspect I loved was that the characters *actually* communicated. Whether it was in a friendship, family, romance, physical or emotional context, they talked to each other and it was great! Anytime I was about to start shouting at them to communicate, they did. It was SO refreshing. <br /><br />Jenn Bennett manages to discuss deeper themes such as PTSD (although not explicitly stated), sex and family breakups in a way that doesn't play on cliché tropes. There's no 'fixing' with romance or totally magical happily ever afters but although it's sometimes heavy, it doesn't weigh you down as Jenn Bennett's writing style is so easy and comfortable to read. With that being said, I would want to add a trigger warning for flashbacks and PTSD (again, this isn't explicitly stated or diagnosed on the page but it's something I'd be wary of if you know you're sensitive to this topic.) <br /><br />Yes, there were some undeniably predictable moments but somehow that didn't take away from my enjoyment whatsoever. Instead I felt like an insider looking in knowing a secret the characters didn't. Jenn Bennett is such an underrated voice in YA and I'm incredibly excited to continue to read and love her book. <br /><br />If you're looking for a perfectly adorable, multi layered, somewhat more mature YA contemporary, Alex, Approximately is one of undoubtably recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="118065044184631985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1892756927?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2019</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34787673-alex-approximately">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1892756927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7673257369393846005">hello i loved this!!! i loved it so much more than i expected to love it, because you know, the reviews were a little off-putting.... <br/><br/>BUT ultimately i am so glad i gave jenn bennett a chance!!<br/><br/>bailey rydell is an evader. she hides from all her problems rather than face them, and is a master at avoiding awkward situations. she often lets events decide the course of her life for her instead of taking action. this book would have been your typical summer romance mixed with You've Got Mail and some f</span>
  <span id="freeText7673257369393846005" style="display:none">hello i loved this!!! i loved it so much more than i expected to love it, because you know, the reviews were a little off-putting.... <br /><br />BUT ultimately i am so glad i gave jenn bennett a chance!!<br /><br />bailey rydell is an evader. she hides from all her problems rather than face them, and is a master at avoiding awkward situations. she often lets events decide the course of her life for her instead of taking action. this book would have been your typical summer romance mixed with You've Got Mail and some film references, except for bailey. she represented and resembled me in a way i couldn't even bring myself to accept until i finished reading. i hate conflict, despise it because i get easily anxious about people's judgment of me. i chronically avoid my life problems, and i'm not even saying that to joke like some people do. honestly i just wait them out until they blow over eventually and then i act like they never happened. i can never for the love of me decide on anything so my biggest motto is "go with the flow" and work around whatever events have just occurred in my life. bailey is me, down to the very bone.<br /><br />the romance: i loved it. so much. porter didn't annoy me at all in fact i want to wrap him in a blanket and protect him. he's been through so much and yet he still emerged even stronger. also he is such a sweet and capable and supportive boyfriend i just T_T<br /><br />in summary: amazing contemporary beach read with deeper layers than you'd expect. personally, it was impactful for me because of how much i resonated with the heroine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7673257369393846005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mcFbLn62gruWBxAt967oexOqcmhKU0o+1wa9OmTFyVpJ3pr7cGTx7juVli6nXxCT6GpS041OkmNdVlBx6Z/BtQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('85qe++6Co1aVQWSE4vgYyvrRJZaIuM8qDzddKUSo+9sjhV8u4FDQAzjT4oeyCeAiAREFLU+lF3eFZ7BiyfLzNA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17126393747114666344">Jenn Bennett is the author of over a dozen books, including the young adult titles: ALEX, APPROXIMATELY; STARRY EYES; SERIOUS MOONLIGHT; and THE LADY ROGUE. She also writes romance and fantasy for adults. Her books have earned multiple starred reviews, been Goodreads Choice Award nominees, and have been included on annual Best Book lists for both Kirkus and Publishers Weekly. She lives near Atlant</span>
  <span id="freeText17126393747114666344" style="display:none">Jenn Bennett is the author of over a dozen books, including the young adult titles: ALEX, APPROXIMATELY; STARRY EYES; SERIOUS MOONLIGHT; and THE LADY ROGUE. She also writes romance and fantasy for adults. Her books have earned multiple starred reviews, been Goodreads Choice Award nominees, and have been included on annual Best Book lists for both Kirkus and Publishers Weekly. She lives near Atlanta with one husband and two dogs. Visit her at <a href="https://www.jennbennett.net" rel="nofollow noopener">www.jennbennett.net</a>.<br /><br />Follow her on:<br /><br /><a href="http://www.twitter.com/jenn_benn" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br /><a href="http://www.instagram.com/j3nn_benn" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br /><br /><br /></span>
